[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m user
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m How many vertical asymptotes does the graph of $y=\frac{2}{x^2+x-6}$ have? Let's think step by step and output the final answer within \boxed{}.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m assistant
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to identify the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero. Vertical asymptotes occur where the function is undefined due to division by zero.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Step 1: Factor the denominator.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The denominator of the function is \( x^2 + x - 6 \). To factor this quadratic expression, we look for two numbers that multiply to \(-6\) and add up to \(1\). These numbers are \(3\) and \(-2\).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, we can factor the quadratic as:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2)
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Step 2: Set the denominator equal to zero.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The function becomes:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m y = \frac{2}{(x + 3)(x - 2)}
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m To find the values of \( x \) that make the function undefined, we set the denominator equal to zero:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Step 3: Solve for \( x \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m We solve the equation using the zero product property:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m x + 3 = 0 \quad \text{or} \quad x - 2 = 0
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m x = -3 \quad \text{or} \quad x = 2
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Step 4: Verify that these values are within the domain of the function.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The values \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \) make the denominator zero, which causes the function to be undefined at these points. Therefore, these are the locations of the vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Step 5: Count the number of vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Since we found two distinct values (\(x = -3\) and \(x = 2\)) that make the denominator zero, there are two vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the graph of \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) has \(\boxed{2}\) vertical asymptotes.

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to identify the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, as these are the points where the function approaches infinity or negative infinity, thus creating vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 1. **Identify the denominator:**
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    The denominator of the function is \( x^2 + x - 6 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 2. **Factor the quadratic expression:**
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    We need to factor the quadratic expression \( x^2 + x - 6 \). We look for two numbers that multiply to \(-6\) and add to \(1\). These numbers are \(3\) and \(-2\). Thus, we can factor the quadratic expression as:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2)
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 3. **Set the factored form to zero:**
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    To find the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, we set each factor equal to zero:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    x + 3 = 0 \quad \text{or} \quad x - 2 = 0
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    Solving these equations, we get:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    x = -3 \quad \text{or} \quad x = 2
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 4. **Determine the vertical asymptotes:**
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    The function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) will have vertical asymptotes at the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero. Therefore, the vertical asymptotes are at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 5. **Count the number of vertical asymptotes:**
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m    There are two distinct values, \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \), which means there are two vertical asymptotes.

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m assistant
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to identify the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, as these values will correspond to the locations of the vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, we factor the denominator:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m We look for two numbers that multiply to \(-6\) and add to \(1\). These numbers are \(3\) and \(-2\). Thus, we can factor the quadratic as:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2). \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Setting the factored form of the denominator equal to zero gives us:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m This equation is satisfied when:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x + 3 = 0 \quad \text{or} \quad x - 2 = 0. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the solutions are:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x = -3 \quad \text{and} \quad x = 2. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m These are the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, and therefore, the potential locations of vertical asymptotes. Since the denominator does not have any repeated factors, these are simple vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Therefore, the graph of \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) has two vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The final answer is:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \boxed{2}

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to find the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, as these are the points where the function is undefined and potentially has vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, we factor the quadratic expression in the denominator:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2). \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m So the function becomes:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ y = \frac{2}{(x + 3)(x - 2)}. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The function will have vertical asymptotes at the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, provided they do not also make the numerator zero. Since the numerator is 2, it is never zero. Therefore, we need to solve:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The solutions to this equation are:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x = -3 \quad \text{and} \quad x = 2. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Since neither of these values are zeros of the numerator, the function has vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) has 2 vertical asymptotes. Therefore, the number of vertical asymptotes is:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ \boxed{2} \]

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, we factor the denominator \( x^2 + x - 6 \):
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2). \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m So the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) can be rewritten as:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ y = \frac{2}{(x + 3)(x - 2)}. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The function is undefined where the denominator is zero, i.e., where \( (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0 \). This occurs at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Therefore, the potential vertical asymptotes are at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \). To confirm that these are indeed vertical asymptotes and not holes, we need to check that these points are not also zeros of the numerator. The numerator of the function is 2, which is never zero. Hence, the points \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \) are vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to identify the values of \( x \) for which the denominator is zero, as these values will make the function undefined and potentially create vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, we factor the denominator:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2). \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the function can be rewritten as:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ y = \frac{2}{(x + 3)(x - 2)}. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The denominator is zero when \( (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0 \). Solving this equation, we get:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x + 3 = 0 \implies x = -3, \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x - 2 = 0 \implies x = 2. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Therefore, the potential vertical asymptotes occur at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m To confirm that these are indeed vertical asymptotes, we need to check that these points do not also make the numerator zero (which would indicate a hole instead of an asymptote). The numerator is 2, which is never zero. Therefore, the points \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \) are vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) has two vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to identify the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, as vertical asymptotes occur where the function is undefined due to division by zero.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, we factorize the denominator \( x^2 + x - 6 \):
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2). \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The function \( y = \frac{2}{(x + 3)(x - 2)} \) is undefined when the denominator is zero, i.e., when \( (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0 \). Solving this equation, we get:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x + 3 = 0 \quad \text{or} \quad x - 2 = 0, \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m which gives us \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m These are the points where the function has vertical asymptotes. Therefore, the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) has vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the number of vertical asymptotes is \( 2 \).

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, we factor the denominator \( x^2 + x - 6 \). We need to solve the quadratic equation \( x^2 + x - 6 = 0 \). This can be factored as follows:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2). \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m So, the denominator factors into \( (x + 3)(x - 2) \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Setting the denominator equal to zero gives us:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m This equation is satisfied when \( x = -3 \) or \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Therefore, the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) has vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \). These are the points where the denominator is zero and the function is undefined.

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes of the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to find the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, as these are the points where the function approaches infinity or negative infinity, creating vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, we factor the denominator:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2). \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Setting the denominator equal to zero gives:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m This equation has solutions:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x + 3 = 0 \quad \text{or} \quad x - 2 = 0, \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m which means:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x = -3 \quad \text{or} \quad x = 2. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m These values, \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \), are the locations of the vertical asymptotes, provided they are not canceled out by any zeros in the numerator. The numerator of the function is \( 2 \), which does not have any \( x \)-values that make it zero. Therefore, the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) will have vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the function has two vertical asymptotes. The answer is:

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to identify the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, as these are the potential locations for vertical asymptotes. 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, let's set the denominator equal to zero and solve for \( x \):
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = 0. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m This is a quadratic equation, and we can factor it:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Setting each factor equal to zero gives us the solutions:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x + 3 = 0 \quad \Rightarrow \quad x = -3, \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x - 2 = 0 \quad \Rightarrow \quad x = 2. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the denominator \( x^2 + x - 6 \) equals zero at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \). Therefore, the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) will have vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \), provided these values do not make the numerator zero.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The numerator of the function is \( 2 \), which is never zero. Therefore, the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) will have vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \).
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the function has two vertical asymptotes.

[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m user
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m How many vertical asymptotes does the graph of $y=\frac{2}{x^2+x-6}$ have? Let's think step by step and output the final answer within \boxed{}.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m assistant
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m [response] To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \), we need to identify the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero, as these are the points where the function is undefined, and potentially where vertical asymptotes occur.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m First, we factor the denominator \( x^2 + x - 6 \):
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x^2 + x - 6 = (x + 3)(x - 2). \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m So, the function can be rewritten as:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ y = \frac{2}{(x + 3)(x - 2)}. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m The function will have vertical asymptotes at the values of \( x \) that make the denominator zero. Setting the denominator equal to zero, we get:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ (x + 3)(x - 2) = 0. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m This gives us the solutions:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x + 3 = 0 \quad \text{or} \quad x - 2 = 0, \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m which are:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ x = -3 \quad \text{and} \quad x = 2. \]
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m These are the potential vertical asymptotes. To confirm, we check that these values do not also make the numerator zero. The numerator is 2, which is never zero. Therefore, the values \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \) are indeed vertical asymptotes.
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m 
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m Thus, the function \( y = \frac{2}{x^2 + x - 6} \) has vertical asymptotes at \( x = -3 \) and \( x = 2 \). Therefore, the number of vertical asymptotes is:
[36m(TaskRunner pid=2892777)[0m \[ \boxed{2}. \]
